They were all taken to the police station for investigation, while detectives were sent to arrest the remaining accomplices.

Zhang Shiying Family Lawsuit Judgment

Regarding the Zhang Shiying family lawsuit, the court has made a judgment. The judgment is recorded as follows: Plaintiff, i.e., counterclaim defendant and incidental civil plaintiff, Zhang Yexiu, female, 39 years old, from Nanjing, residing at No. 13 Mingwa Lane, represented by lawyers Xu Bingcheng and Xu Fuji. Defendant, i.e., counterclaim plaintiff, Zhang Shiying, male, 55 years old, from Hefei, residing at No. 37 Zhangjiabang, salt merchant, represented by lawyer Zhang Shizhao. The defendant in the above case was sued by the plaintiff for breach of trust and embezzlement, with incidental civil claim. The defendant also filed a counterclaim. The court's judgment is as follows: (Ruling) Zhang Shiying is not guilty. Zhang Yexiu is not guilty. The incidental civil claim part is transferred to the civil court of this court for trial. (Reasons) According to this case, the defendant, i.e., the counterclaim plaintiff, Zhang Shiying, and the plaintiff's husband, i.e., the counterclaim defendant, Zhang Shikun, are brothers. Shikun has been ill for a long time. Since the separation in the eighth year of the Republic of China [1919], he has entrusted the defendant to manage his property. The income and expenditure over the years have been recorded in ledgers. However, the expenditures are too large, and there have been instances of pledging and selling property. The plaintiff therefore believes that there has been a breach of trust and embezzlement and filed a lawsuit. The defendant also filed a counterclaim for false accusation. After repeated summons, the defendant has submitted all the detailed ledgers of income and expenditure over the years for Langji (i.e., under Shikun's name) and Anji (i.e., the common house of each room), the list of sold fields and houses of Langji, the detailed ledger of each house's pond project, and the ledger of capital and profit and loss of Yihexing Salt Shop and the property deeds of the ninth room (i.e., under Shikun's name). After reviewing the accounts, they were all signed by Zhang Shikun or the plaintiff. It can be seen that there is no fraud. Although the plaintiff stated that one payment of 4,300 yuan in the 13th year and a pledge of 5,000 yuan in the 18th year were not received, the ledgers are all available for review. Moreover, an accountant has settled the accounts. It is clear that this case is purely a family dispute that has led to a misunderstanding. The defendant has not committed any breach of trust or embezzlement. The plaintiff cannot be said to have made a deliberate false accusation. As for the incidental civil claim part, there are still points to be investigated and should be transferred to the relevant court of this court for trial. Therefore, according to Articles 316 and 510 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the judgment is as stated in the ruling. If you are not satisfied with the judgment, you may appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court within ten days from the day after the service of the judgment. December 18, 20th year of the Republic of China [1931], First Special District Court of Shanghai, Jiangsu, Criminal Court Judge Shen Bingrong, on the Huahai Wheel.

Large-Scale Child Trafficking Case Uncovered

Liu Jinfu, a police officer of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team, and detective Yang Chunting, were patrolling by patrol boat around 9:00 PM the day before yesterday. Near the Dada Pier, they saw the Huaan ship bound for Fujian, which was docked there and had not yet set sail. They boarded the ship to conduct an inspection. They found the following individuals in the cabins: Chen Wang, carrying a boy; Chen Lin, carrying a girl; Chen Gao, carrying a boy and a girl; Chen Ren, carrying a boy; Cai Chen, carrying a boy; Cao Bingnan, carrying a boy; Chen Deyuan and his wife Lin, carrying a boy. In total, there were two men, six women, six boys, and two girls. Their behavior was suspicious. They were all taken to the team. Xu, the captain, presided over the preliminary examination. Chen Wang stated that she was 22 years old, from Zhenjiang, and lived at No. 20 Yicheng Lane, South Wharf. Her husband's name is Chen Asan, and he is a soldier on a famous ship. The boy she was carrying is named Xizi, and he is seven years old. She bought him for 80 yuan and planned to take him to Fujian. Cao Bingnan stated that he was 31 years old, from Zhenjiang, and lived at No. 26 Haichao Temple Street, outside Xiaonanmen, South City. The boy he was carrying is named Zhu Xiaolong, and he is seven years old. Because his father's family is very poor and unable to raise him, he gave him to him. He plans to take him to Fujian. Chen Gao stated that she was 21 years old, from Fujian. The boy she was carrying is five years old, and the girl is just one year old. She bought the boy for 70 yuan and the girl for only 15 yuan. She plans to take them all to Fujian. Chen Deyuan stated that he was 38 years old, from Fujian. His wife, Lin, is 37 years old. The boy they were carrying is named Asheng, and he is two years old. His remaining words were vague. Chen Ren stated that she was 51 years old, from Fujian. The boy she was carrying is two years old, and she bought him for 21 yuan. Cai Chen stated that she was 51 years old, from Fujian. Her remaining words were vague. Chen Lin stated that she was 43 years old, from Fujian, and lived on Lafayette Road in the French Concession. The girl she was carrying is named Zhang Shuchun, and she is nine years old. She bought her from a neighbor for 120 yuan. Zhang Shuchun said that she was not trafficked by the woman, but by another man who sold her to the woman. At this time, the child's mother, Zhang Xu, heard the news and reported the case, stating that she was 50 years old, from Ningbo. Shuchun is her daughter, and she was trafficked by a former tenant, Su Tongyi, on the 20th of last month. As the case involves a large-scale trafficking of eight boys and girls and is of great importance, in addition to sending Chen Wang's boy Xizi, Chen Lin's girl Zhang Shuchun, Cao Bingnan's boy Zhu Xiaolong, and the plaintiff Zhang Xu to the Shanghai District Court, Chen Gao's boy and girl, Chen Deyuan and Lin's boy Asheng, Chen Ren's boy, and Cai Chen's boy were also sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Zhao Cuilin Sues Stepmother for Inheritance Division

Court Adjourns to Attempt Reconciliation

Zhao Cuilin, a local woman, 23 years old, recently hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Wu Baotai to file a lawsuit with the Civil Court of the First Special District Court, requesting to divide the inheritance with her stepmother, Zhao Lu. The lawsuit stated that the inheritance was being seized and requested a judgment for division. The plaintiff's father, Gui Sheng, had one son and two daughters during his lifetime. The eldest is the plaintiff, Cuilin, the second is the younger sister Linmei, and the third is the younger brother Jingen. After the plaintiff's mother, Shen, passed away, the father married Lu, the defendant, as his stepmother, who only had one daughter. When the father passed away from illness, the property left behind, estimated to be worth 100,000 yuan, was entirely controlled by the defendant. The plaintiff was not given any necessary expenses and was not shown any sympathy despite facing livelihood difficulties. This was intentional mistreatment. The plaintiff, as the eldest daughter, should have the right to inherit according to law. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit requesting that the defendant be ordered to appear in court and that the defendant be ordered to give the plaintiff one-quarter of the inheritance of the late father Gui Sheng, totaling 25,000 yuan, and bear the litigation costs. Furthermore, as the plaintiff is currently facing livelihood difficulties and all property is seized by the defendant, she is unable to pay the litigation costs. In addition to filing a separate guarantee letter to apply for litigation assistance, she also requests that the court approve it. Yesterday morning, Judge Li Mo opened the Ninth Civil Court for interrogation. The defendant hired lawyer Chen Bingxing to appear in court and defend. After the interrogation by Judge Li, it was determined that both parties had hope for reconciliation, so the hearing was adjourned and reconciliation will be attempted first.

Sixth District Police Station

Breaking the Case of the Zhoujiaqiao Bandits

On the afternoon of the 22nd (twenty-second) at approximately 8:40 PM, the Huangjinji Yellow Sand and Gravel Factory, located at No. 27 Gujia Lane, Zhoujiaqiao, West Shanghai, was suddenly stormed by a large group of bandits. They robbed over a thousand silver dollars and dozens of pieces of silk and fur clothing. The responsible Sixth District Police Station, under District Chief Ren, quickly solved the case within four hours, directing officers and detectives. The details are recorded below:

The Robbery Situation The Huangjinji Yellow Mud and Gravel Factory, located at No. 27 Gujia Lane, Zhoujiaqiao, West Shanghai, is owned by Huang Qibao from Teng County, Shandong Province. The business was doing reasonably well. The day before, it was the time to pay the workers' wages. Huang Qibao came to Shanghai in the afternoon and obtained over a thousand silver dollars in cash from a certain bank. He immediately sent someone to take it back to the factory. Huang stayed in Shanghai due to business and planned to return to the factory to pay the wages after 9 PM. Unexpectedly, just after 9:30 PM, eight or nine bandits suddenly burst in, holding pistols, intimidating everyone and forbidding them from making a sound. Two bandits stood guard outside, while the remaining bandits ransacked the place. They robbed 1,070 silver dollars in cash, over thirty pieces of silk, fur, wool, unlined, lined, and cotton cloth clothing, a suitcase, and a bicycle. After obtaining the loot, the bandits fled in all directions. Upon hearing the alarm, Patrol Officer Wei of the Second Sub-station of the Sixth District immediately led all the officers to pursue and arrest them, but the bandits had already gone far. He immediately reported to the Sixth District Public Security Bureau.

Swift Case Solving Upon receiving the report, District Chief Ren of the Sixth District immediately directed Patrol Officer Xu, along with legal police chief Jin Zhang, police officers Liu Changdao, Yang Kunshan, Zhao Changxiu, Detective Team Leader Liu Shaoqing, detectives Gan Youjin, Tang Bingxiang, Cao Chuqiao, Wu Rui, and others, all fully armed, to Zhoujiaqiao to conduct a thorough search. At approximately 1 AM yesterday, Patrol Officer Xu, Patrol Officer Wei, and the legal police chief were patrolling along Avenue Petain when they suddenly saw three rickshaws speeding towards them. One of the people in the rickshaws was covering his face with his hat, looking panicked. They immediately ordered the rickshaws to stop. Unexpectedly, one of the men in the rickshaws drew a gun first, jumped out of the rickshaw in a panic, and fled. The police officers chased after him and apprehended him near Route Tenant de la Tour. They fired a pistol into the air. The bandit, panicking, ran into a small alley and was captured. Along with two other bandits, they were arrested and taken back to the police station. Confessing Accomplices After District Chief Ren interrogated the three bandits, one confessed his name was Wu Jinshan, 26 years old, from Suqian, came from Suzhou, and had previously committed robbery. Another confessed his name was Guo Yongqing, 21 years old, from Suqian, lived at No. 1, Alley, South Yinghua Lane, and was a rickshaw puller. Another confessed his name was Chen Tongsheng, 43 years old, from Siyang, lived in Da Xu Lane, and was a rickshaw puller. All admitted to conspiring to rob the Huangjinji factory of cash and clothing and confessed that there were six accomplices, who were hiding in the first house in No. 1 Da Xu Lane, near Robison Road. Continued Capture of Bandits Yesterday at approximately 8 AM, Patrol Officer Wei led police officers in Zhoujiaqiao to capture a bandit involved in the case, Peng Shangzheng, and recovered nine pieces of stolen goods, including a woolen serge cheongsam. He was immediately escorted to the Sixth District Police Station. Also, at approximately 11 AM, Patrol Officer Xu, along with detectives and detectives dispatched by the Putuo Road Police Station, went to Da Xu Lane and arrested five bandits and one female bandit on the spot. They seized a pistol, several bullets, over thirty pieces of original stolen goods, including silk, fur, cotton, single-layer, and gauze clothing, a leather suitcase, and a bicycle. They were immediately taken back together. The factory owners, Huang Qibao and Huang Qiyun, identified all the stolen goods as correct. After District Chief Ren interrogated the bandits, one confessed his name was Chen Yishun, 34 years old, from Xuzhou. Another confessed his name was Xia Yuansheng, 25 years old, from Suqian. Another confessed her name was Hou Guiying, 32 years old, from Xuzhou. Another confessed his name was Wei Qinggao, 36 years old, from Suqian. Another confessed his name was Hou Guiyou, 26 years old, from Xuzhou. The female, Hou Li, 37 years old, from Suqian, all admitted to the robbery. After obtaining the confessions, District Chief Ren prepared a document in the afternoon and sent it to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Public Telephones to Be Increased in This City

Merchants Can Request to Manage Them

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications has already set up public telephones in the city, including the South Shanghai Main Bureau, the North Zhabei First and Second Sub-bureaus, the Jiangwan Sub-bureau, and the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank’s Old West Gate and Small East Gate sub-branches, totaling six locations. The Municipal Public Utility Bureau believes that these telephones are a convenient tool for public transportation. Given the vast area of the city, the large population, and the high demand for telephones, the bureau believes that only six locations are insufficient to meet the needs. Therefore, it proposed recruiting merchants in suitable locations to manage the telephones on its behalf, offering generous rewards to facilitate promotion. It drafted measures for merchants to manage public telephones and sent them to the Shanghai Telephone Bureau for consideration. It has now been learned that the measures have been submitted to the Ministry of Communications for approval. Merchants in commercially important areas of the city can request the Shanghai Telephone Bureau to install public telephones and manage them.

Li Yunsheng's Home Robbed

The home of Li Yunsheng, located at No. 33 Suozi Lane, south of Dengyun Bridge, Zhaojiabang Road, Shanghai, was hosting a winter solstice banquet for relatives and friends the day before (the 22nd). At 7:30 PM, eight bandits suddenly arrived. Three bandits stood guard outside, and five bandits entered, four wearing grey overcoats and long gowns, and one wearing short clothes. All held pistols and claimed to be there to search for opium. They first ordered everyone to remain silent, then drove Li's entire family and the visiting relatives and friends, as well as Li's three tenants, into one room, which they locked and guarded. The bandits then went upstairs to the bedrooms, ransacked the place, and searched and robbed at will before leaving with their loot. Afterwards, the stolen items were inventoried, including a total of 400 large and small new and old glass beads (for bead flowers) belonging to the Ye family, four gold rings inlaid with jewels, 80 silver dollars, a gold lock pendant with a chain and chicken heart pendant belonging to the Shen family, another ring, and 74 silver dollars. Li's home was reported to have not been robbed because the bandits thought they were taking too long and feared something might happen, so they did not search Li's bedroom. All the victims reported the robbery to the Second Sub-station of the Second District, requesting that the police investigate the stolen goods and bring the robbers to justice.

Cheng Zanhua Escapes and Is Recaptured

Cheng Zanping, a 26-year-old from Shandong, claimed to have studied at Shanghai West University, but did not graduate. He then became an investigator for the Stamp Tax Bureau but lost his job. He drifted into a group of thieves and gradually became bold. He even stole firearms from the Jinghu Railway North Station Police Department, hoping to get a good price. He was arrested by railway police and detained in a detention center. Cheng's hands were shackled, but he took advantage of the guards' negligence and, with the shackles still on, climbed the fence like a monkey and escaped. As a result, the guard, Zhuang Ziquan, was escorted by the police department to the local court for questioning. However, after Cheng escaped, he hid in the Xin Luming Hotel on the Fourth Road. The police department found out and, together with the patrol station, arrested Cheng. Yesterday, he was transferred to the local court for questioning.

Worker Falls and Dies Tragically

Qin Binghua, an 18-year-old from Pudong, was working as a construction worker at the Huangpu Wharf of the Yangshupu Twisting Flower Bureau. Yesterday at approximately 12 PM, he was working on the roof of a building approximately 40 feet above the ground when he accidentally fell from a high place, injuring vital parts of his body and dying instantly. The fire department used a vehicle to transport him to Tongren Hospital and then to the coroner's office to await inspection by the court.

Lawsuit for Negligence and Endangering Life

Rescheduled Due to Defendant's Absence

Cen Ziliang, a local resident and manager of the Xu Chongdao Pharmacy on Avenue Edward VII, was recently sued by Li Xin, a Suzhou resident living at No. 23 Jingzhao Lane, Santeli, Avenue Mepleg, who retained lawyers Gao Wenqi and Zhang Ding to file a complaint with the First Special District Court for negligence and endangering life. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Feng Shide presided over the hearing in the Second Criminal Court. The defendant, Cen Ziliang, was absent and sent a lawyer to request a postponement. The plaintiff, Li Jinsheng, testified that he was a jeweler and explained the situation. He also stated that his wife had hired a Western doctor for treatment and that, due to mistakenly taking the prescription, she had entered the second stage of lung disease. If not treated promptly, it would be incurable by next year. His attorney stated that the defendant had committed the crime of negligent injury under Article 301, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Code and submitted all the evidence and the reply from the Shenzhou National Medical Association. Judge Feng reviewed the case and stated that the person responsible for the incorrect prescription should be determined urgently to assign responsibility. Since the defendant was absent, the judge adjourned the hearing to Monday afternoon of next week. If the defendant fails to appear again, a warrant will be issued for his arrest.

Reactions to Rent Increase in Pucheng and C'ian Lanes

The houses in Pucheng and C'ian Lanes on Route Lafayette in the French Concession are owned by Pua'itang and managed by the China Business Company. The rent was increased once in 1929. After repeated requests from the tenants, Father Jin verbally agreed to temporarily increase the rent by 4% and reconsider the situation after five years. However, Father Jin had just returned to his country this summer when the company issued a notice to all tenants this month, stating that the rent would be increased by 30% starting in January 1932. The tenants of both lanes believe that, in the face of the current national crisis and economic depression, it is difficult to bear the increased burden. They have organized a tenants' meeting and sent a letter to the company, requesting that the rent increase be cancelled.

Essentials of Social Insurance Are Popular

Mr. Zhang Xiaolin's eldest son, Fa Yao, studied in France for several years and is proficient in literature. In addition to his studies, he devoted himself to writing and authored the book "Essentials of Social Insurance." He analyzes in detail the seven aspects of social insurance: disasters, illnesses, pregnancy, disability, death, old age, and unemployment. The book is published by the Huatong Bookstore in this city. The preface includes inscriptions and recommendations from Yu Youren, Wang Zhengting, Wang Chonghui, Zhang Shizhao, Tang Yi, and other celebrities. All major bookstores are selling it, and buyers are rushing to purchase it. Mr. Zhang has recently written a book on finance and economics, which will be published soon.

Minutes of the Shareholders' Meeting of the Dongfang Automobile Company

The Dongfang Automobile Company held its second annual shareholders' meeting at 2 PM yesterday on the second floor of No. 439 Rue Bayle in the French Concession. Shareholders Ma Hongji, Hu Gongji, Chen Rupin, Ying Rongfu, Hu Linbao, He Shishang, Hu Hanchen, Hu Zhikang, Gu Zhaofu, Xu Lusheng, Ge Zhentai, Gu Xianbi, Hu Xiaozhi, Hu Benzhi, Ye Chuangen, Gu Guan'gen, and others were present. Ying Rongfu was elected as the temporary chairman. The meeting was conducted in accordance with protocol. Chen Rupin reported on the company's business situation. Ma Hongji and Hu Gongji were elected as directors, Chen Rupin as supervisor, Ying Rongfu as manager, and Hu Linbao as assistant manager. The meeting adjourned at 5 PM with refreshments.

Honor of Dr. Ge Yangmin

Dr. Ge Yangmin, a director of the National Medical Center, has profound medical knowledge. Those treated by her have found her medicine to be effective. Recently, it was heard that the elderly mother of the Zhang family in Datiebang, who is over sixty years old, suffered from a severe case of typhoid fever. Her lips were parched and her tongue was black. She urgently asked Dr. Ge to come for treatment, and she recovered within a few days. The whole family celebrated. It was also heard that wealthy merchant Zhu Xianhuai presented her with a plaque yesterday, which was delivered by his daughter, Miss Jinghe. The inscription read "Gentle and Harmonious Reunion." Dr. Ge currently has clinics at No. 6 Puyuli, Penglai Road, West Gate, and Room 318, 4th Floor, Zhonghe Building, No. 74 Shanxi Road, Nanjing Road.

Christmas Dinner at the Home Restaurant

The Home Restaurant at No. 296 Rue de Sieyes is conveniently located diagonally opposite the entrance of the Racecourse. It has excellent seating, elegant furnishings, and attentive service. The chef hired is the former Western chef of the Dahua Hotel, hired by the owner, Mr. He Zhaoyu, at a high price. Therefore, the Western cuisine is the best in Shanghai. Today and tomorrow are Christmas Day, and the restaurant is offering special Western dishes, including the famous turkey. For the sake of valued regular customers, the price will not be increased and will remain at the original price of $1.50 per person. Last night, Mr. He Zhaoyu invited members of the press to sample the food in advance. Many prominent members of the press attended and praised the unexpected flavors, freshness, and deliciousness. The hosts and guests enjoyed themselves until 10 PM.

Giant Film Premieres in Nanjing (The Constant Nymph)

The tragic and charming giant film (The Constant Nymph), starring movie queen Janet Gaynor and movie emperor Charles Farrell, is the best work since (Seventh Heaven). The plot is full of twists and turns and is extremely sad. Janet's performance is exceptionally delicate and profound. It is said that the film is scheduled to premiere at the Nanjing Grand Theater starting today.

Anlu Extended Discount

The 30% discount sale at the Anlu Cotton Weaving Factory on Nanjing Road has expired and will be extended for another seven days.

Looking for Missing Child Mao Xinggen

Mao Xiaofu, a resident of Shaoxing, lives at the Huayang Teahouse at the intersection of Xinmin Road and Huasheng Road in Zhabei and works as a worker at the Shanghai Brewery. His son, Xinggen, who is seven years old, went missing yesterday afternoon. He has been searched for everywhere but cannot be found. When the child went missing, he had a bald head, wore a floral Zhigong cotton robe, and a red-striped factory cloth long gown. He wore a white head rope around his neck and gray cloth cotton shoes with white edges. Mao Xiaofu is heartbroken due to his love for his son and is in great distress. He hopes that anyone who has taken in this child will quickly send him to the address so that the family can be reunited.

Bethel Mission Report on the Northeast Incident

The circumnavigating mission team organized by the Bethel Christian Church outside the West Gate of this city went to preach in various parts of the Northeast at the end of August. It happened to encounter the invasion of the Japanese invaders. The delegation preached in important locations in Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang for three months. After careful investigation, it witnessed the impact on the churches, the oppression of the schools, and the innocent deaths of compatriots. The delegation personally witnessed the brutality and unreasonableness of the Japanese, the occupation of the territory, and the seizure of national rights. It was filled with grief. Since returning to Shanghai, it has been reporting the true situation in the Northeast in various churches. Those who hear it are moved. The delegation deeply feels the lack of national spirit and the cowardice of the military. At this time of being watched by powerful neighbors, when the national spirit cannot be extended, it wants to invigorate itself, recover its territory, and resist foreign insults. The only way to do this is through moral transformation to eliminate corrupt officials and cowardly soldiers. All believers should not only pray for the country but also work hard to spread the message to save the country. In order to train missionaries, the delegation has decided to establish a short-term Bible course for one month starting on February 3 next year. All Christians who wish to attend are welcome. Inquiries about the details will be answered.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather in the Yangtze River Basin and coastal areas would be cloudy and colder. There would be snow in the north of the Yellow Sea. Shandong and the coastal areas of the country would have strong seasonal winds from the northwest to northeast. Also, the highest temperature in this city in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday was 50.0 degrees, and the lowest was 36.7 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 41.7 degrees, and the lowest was 27.3 degrees.

Reader's Letter

Mr. Peinong's Message (The Minimum Anti-Japanese Work)

Since the Japanese invaders invaded our eastern provinces, three months have passed. All of our citizens are furious and enraged. Everywhere is sufficient to show the true awakening of our people, no longer the five-minute fever of the past. Even if we take the boycott of Japanese goods as an example, the Japanese have reduced their exports by hundreds of millions of dollars to date, resulting in losses of no less than several million dollars. All of this is enough to frustrate the arrogance of the Japanese and save the country in the slightest. It is also a manifestation of our national spirit and the result of single-minded efforts. However, foreign disasters have not diminished as a result. There are still many things that our people should strive for. We all know that since the Opium War, for decades, under the balance of power of foreigners, all kinds of political and economic aggression have been used to the extreme. The September 18th Incident was even worse. We are under the watchful eyes of tigers. The wounds are deep, the pain is extreme, and the disease has penetrated the bone marrow and cannot be cured. This is the wish of the imperialists and the critical moment for our country's survival. However, as long as the spirit of China is not dead for a day and the lifeline of the country is still there for a day, all of our compatriots should take the most effective methods to confront them and continue to work hard to achieve it for the sake of the country and the nation. What is the most effective method? It is the aggression of foreigners and the economic aggression. Even its political aggression is economic aggression. The most effective method is naturally to制之control it with economy. All of the following are the most economical means that our compatriots should adopt, and they are also the efforts that can achieve the greatest results with the slightest effort: (1) Absolute boycott of Japanese goods. Although this is already underway, since Japan recently implemented a gold re-ban, its purpose is nothing more than to develop trade in China. The Japanese have seen through our country's boycott as a temporary fever, and most people are greedy for profit. Therefore, in order to avoid being tricked, we should make a thorough boycott of Japanese goods and embrace the spirit of "Don't want it even if it's cheaper," regardless of whether it's a necessity or a luxury. (2) Don't buy foreign goods other than indispensable commodities. On the one hand, prevent the outflow of 利權 rights, and on the other hand, promote domestic goods. Foreign goods are more expensive, and in general, fashionable people are all "Westernized" in their minds, so domestic goods are in danger. This point should include two things: (A) Don't buy luxury goods. (B) Don't buy foreign goods if there are domestic goods that can replace them. (3) Strive to promote domestic goods and實業 industry. (A) Government encouragement and protection. (B) Media promotion. (C) Investment efforts. (D) Awakening of the people. This point is the most important. To this day, the reason why domestic goods have declined is that domestic merchants cannot compete with foreigners. The biggest reasons are as follows: (甲) the constraints of unequal treaties; (乙) the lack of capital. Both of these reasons are sufficient to affect the cost of production, and 間拉 between enough to affect the price of production. As a result, for the same goods, if our country's merchants make it, the cost will be expensive, and if foreign merchants make it, the cost will be cheap. However, patriotic merchants will not regret it. All success or failure depends on us. If our compatriots can have true awareness and can be considerate of domestic goods, then even if foreign goods are 精 refined and cheap, and domestic goods are 拙 clumsy and expensive,寧捨 rather give up foreign goods and choose domestic goods, then imperialists will fall without being attacked. Then China's domestic goods are almost achieved. (4) Cultivate the habit of frugality. People in the cities mostly admire the European style, but in fact, it is all superficial. The so-called "modern" clothing must be Western-style suits, food must be Western food, living must be 洋房 Western-style houses, and transportation must be automobiles. They waste money to gain vanity and waste time and abandon practicality. We all know that Gandhi in a Western suit is despised, while Gandhi in coarse cloth is respected. People don't have to be judged by their clothes, and people don't have to be 洋 Westernized in their腔 accent to be 摩登 modern. Moreover, these kinds of enjoyment are mostly畸形 deformed and not in line with China's national conditions. If we think of the victims of disaster in the sixteen provinces who are waiting to be fed and仰天 howling in the cold, they are also people, and we are also people. The difference in experience is self-evident. If we can truly save the world and truly love people, save a few coins, cultivate the habit of frugality, and invest in民 industry, then people's welfare will depend on it, and the revitalization of domestic goods will have a day. If it is so, it is better than building a seven-story pagoda. (5) Eliminate the custom of sending festival gifts and New Year's greetings. Regarding this level, when we think about the motivation, it is nothing more than using this on the one hand to "connect emotions" and on the other hand to use this as a "happy thing." However, in this time of national crisis, when there is no time for sorrow, how can there be happiness? As for connecting emotions, then the emotions that need to be connected by gifts are also not good and not wonderful. Moreover, in reality, those who send gifts are often not economically裕餘 surplus. In severe cases, they even borrow money to send gifts to make friends with people. From the perspective of the giver, the situation is indeed unbearable. Even from the perspective of the receiver, the favor is also difficult to bear. Moreover, the gifts sent by the giver are mostly foreign goods or useless items. This is tantamount to creating sales channels for foreigners, and the useful money is used for unnecessary items. It is most effective to send each other gifts and reduce the utility of money. What is even worse is that general male and female students use their parents' hard-earned money to exchange worthless gifts to create emotions and gain vanity. This is the behavior of gold-worshippers and should not be taken. Not only that, young students are the most promising for the country. Customs like this, which are harmful to the family and the country, should be eliminated. Chinese people, why don't we all do it together? Don't use unconscious actions at one time to follow this and trap the country in decline.

Correspondence

To the Esteemed Editor,

Having recently read in your esteemed newspaper the Nanjing dispatch stating that Shao Gu went to Taiyuan on the 22nd to urge Feng to come to Beijing to participate in the plenary session, Gu yesterday came to Shanghai due to illness to seek medical treatment at the Hua Xia Fei Sanatorium. The talk of going to Jin is completely untrue. Please correct this matter. With best regards, Huang Shao Gu respectfully. December 23rd.

Respectfully,

Having read the news item published in the local news column of your esteemed newspaper on December 23rd ("The branch offices of various districts in this city held a joint meeting yesterday"), the inclusion of our branch office as attending the meeting is quite perplexing. Upon investigation, our branch office has not held a meeting or sent representatives to participate in any organization since the 25th Party Member Congress on the 11th of this month. This record is likely incorrect. In addition to reporting our denial, we hope you will correct this matter. This is of utmost importance. Please accept the respects of the Shanghai Special Municipality Sixth District Twenty-fourth Branch of the Chinese Nationalist Party. December 23rd.

Respectfully,

Having read today's local news column in your esteemed newspaper regarding the joint meeting of various district branch offices, it mentioned that our branch office attended. Upon investigation, our branch office did not participate in the joint meeting. Fearing this may cause confusion, we hereby solemnly declare this and hope it can be published in the correspondence column for correction. With best wishes, the Eighteenth Branch of the Second District of the Shanghai Special Municipality of the Chinese Nationalist Party. December 23rd.

Having recently read in your esteemed newspaper a news item about the joint meeting of the branch offices of various districts in this city, which listed the Sixth, Sixth, Seventh, Eighth, Ninth, and Tenth branches of the Sixth District as participating, we are extremely astonished. Upon investigation, our branch offices have always adhered to Party discipline and have never participated in any recent organizations or meetings. Fearing this may cause confusion, in addition to publishing a statement, we are sending this special letter, hoping for a correction. Respectfully addressed to the esteemed editor of the Shen Bao newspaper. The Sixth, Sixth, Seventh, Eighth, Ninth, and Tenth branches of the Sixth District of the Shanghai Special Municipality of the Chinese Nationalist Party, together. Addressed to the esteemed editor of the Shen Bao newspaper.

Youth Garden

Private Tutor

— Ding Nu

(One)

It could be considered his fortune that he completed his university education at a time when the world economy was in a state of panic. However, the scent of the petty bourgeoisie became an obstacle to his attainment of so-called academic achievement. And the strict and insurmountable walls of society just so happened to limit his path after leaving school. In this hodgepodge situation, he became a bored private tutor.

Although drinking too much alcohol is certainly uncomfortable, not drinking enough is not comfortable either. Therefore, since he took up the teaching post, he has not felt any less bored than when he was idle. When he has nothing to do, he always wants to find something to do, just as when the sky is overcast, one always hopes for the sunlight to come out to freshen the air. But when the sunlight really shines through, it is not necessarily pleasant. At that time, your discomfort may be because the light is too strong or too weak. The world never fully achieves an ideal state in one fell swoop. In history, there have been many figures we admire who lived very difficult lives before they became prominent. When he reached the extreme of depression, he had to use these theories as temporary comfort. Apart from the present, he is also at a loss when it comes to the future.

When he was at school, he had plans for how to arrange his life after leaving school. But when he actually went out into society, he became flustered and helpless. From the experience of reality, he knew that those plans were just a fantasy. In the scientific world of the twentieth century, people who harbor fantasies simply cannot exist. It is appropriate to be disillusioned by reality. He basically recognized his fate, put down the golden ax of hope, and surrendered to this society. It is pitiful that he is like a statue waiting to be bound by the dragon, a godless believer with no autonomy.

In front of society, he displayed his incompetence, but in front of his old acquaintances, he did not have the courage to surrender to society and expose his weaknesses. These two different forces fought in his mind. At first, he was at a loss as to the origin of this war. When he went deeper, he realized that this was due to the reflection of the transitional period between the old and new eras on the one hand, and the petty bourgeoisie's sense of honor pulling the strings on the other. He often thought that if he was a middle school student, it would not matter. But for a dignified college student to do this unpromising thing would be a great loss of face. Otherwise, if he came from a poor family, it would not matter either. Getting thirty dollars a month would not be considered bad luck. But with the status of a petty bourgeoisie, if he was a student, this thirty dollars would only be enough for one splurge, which would be extremely unlucky. Therefore, in front of friends, he was always afraid to say what he was doing. Sometimes, when friends pressed him so hard that he had to answer, he had to say, "I have nothing to do." He thought that it was better to say that he had nothing to do than to say that he was a private tutor. Saying that he had nothing to do was enough to show that his talent had not yet been priced. Saying that he was a private tutor was clearly declaring that the price he had been marked at was too low. (Two)

Watching the wheels of time roll backward while doing something unpromising, he felt sad.

With a shadow of sadness, he walked past the department store. He saw the Christmas gifts displayed beautifully in the glass cabinet, one by one. He sized them up for a long time, hesitating to leave. He was extremely frustrated, thinking that he had no power to buy these gifts to give to some close friends. Last Christmas, he spent more than twenty dollars on things to give to a female friend named Yu and several male classmates. Among these male classmates, the one named Wu received the most. Now, this classmate named Wu has returned to his home in Hong Kong. He has a Western-style house to live in and beautiful lovers to embrace. His life is naturally much more comfortable than his own, but fate is the same. He heard that he was recently ordered by his father to go to a bank to intern. He wrote in a letter that he was not used to it at all. Although it was called going to intern, in fact he only watched people busy coming and going, while he shook his legs and smoked. When the hour came, he put on his hat and left, mixed in the ranks of busy people. The airs were full, but the empty shell of life was hard to bear.

From his classmate Wu, he then thought of his female friend named Yu. He remembered when they lived on North Sichuan Road last winter, this female friend often came to play, and how fun it was. He loved her very much, loved her charming eyes, how . One night, everyone drank some alcohol, and in a drunken state, she opened her delicate throat and sang a song of Wujiapo. This song penetrated his heart and made him so infatuated that he could not wait to step forward and kiss her passionately. The warm memories made him admire this female friend even more. However, the falling flowers have feelings, but the flowing water is merciless. This female friend has been snatched away by a relative of hers, which is not at all frustrating.

Back in his room, his mind was full of cluttered thoughts. One moment it was as if he was in the crowded intersection of a street, the next moment it was as if he was on top of a snowy and icy mountain.

Christmas is coming soon, and he is anxious about it. He hopes to raise a small sum of money as he wishes, so that he can go to the dance hall on Christmas Eve and have a good dance. But looking at the situation, it seems that he will be disappointed. He wants to write a few articles to exchange for some money, but he can't write them. At the same time, the family money that he had been hoping for has not yet arrived, making people wonder if it has been sent, and even if it has been sent, whether it will be in time for use. Such worries oppress him like an ant on a hot pot.

It was not until a friend saw his mood and promised to help him raise this small sum of money that he felt at ease. (Three)

These days, the weather has turned cold, and the north wind is blowing hard again. He can't go outside to walk around, so he has to hide in his attic. But after all, the weather is too cold. Even with talking and laughing, he doesn't feel comfortable. From this time on, he had the idea of installing a stove in his room to spend the winter comfortably. Because of this problem, he frowned again. Although installing a stove does not require much money, it is absolutely impossible under his financial situation. He can only get a salary of thirty yuan a month. Apart from paying rent and food, the rest is limited. There is no surplus to be used for other purposes, so he began to become annoyed again. This evening, he returned from tutoring at the mansion at ten o'clock. It was raining outside.

The raindrops on his sparse black hair trembled in the dim light, and his face looked even paler. He took off his wet clothes and slumped into a chair, starting to gasp for breath.

His lifeless eyes looked around the room for a week, then fell on the picture of a celebrity hanging on the opposite wall. This celebrity is smiling at him. He recognizes that this smile is not well-intentioned, as if saying, the national crisis is coming, and you are still indulging in warm memories and seeking a comfortable personal life, damn it.

Book and Newspaper Reviews

Rice, Cotton, Yarn (Continued) Qin Jiannan

Commodity Series, Volumes 1, 2, and 3

Edited by the Shanghai Bank Investigation Department

Three, Yarn

The section on (Yarn) is the most extensive, with over two hundred pages, and the discussion is also the most detailed. Its structure is similar to the previous two sections, divided into the following sections: (1) Types of Shanghai Cotton Yarn, explaining the meaning of count, types of count, and classification of trademarks; (2) Estimation of Supply and Demand of Shanghai Cotton Yarn, with an annual supply of over 1.2 million bales, of which ten are shipped overseas, 700,000 are shipped to various ports in China, and over 400,000 are used by large and small weaving factories in the city; (3) Transportation and Sale of Shanghai Cotton Yarn, describing the nature of various merchant groups and customs declarations, transportation costs, and the nature of sales, and attaching the position of Shanghai cotton yarn in China's cotton yarn trade; (4) Transactions of Shanghai Cotton Yarn, divided into yarn shops, cotton yarn brokers, foreign firms, exchanges, and brokers; (5) Shanghai Yarn Factories, describing their history, organization, machinery, and operations; (6) Finance of Shanghai Yarn Industry, listing all methods of fundraising in the yarn industry; (7) Value of Shanghai Cotton Yarn, collecting statistics from over ten years, analyzing in detail to obtain long-term trends and reasons for various changes; (8) Shanghai Yarn Industry Groups; (9) Directions for Improvement of Shanghai Yarn Industry, discussing points for improvement for merchant groups, yarn shops, and yarn factories.

There are many excellent points in the book, and I will mention a few for introduction.

(1) Special attention is paid to the sales of various brands of cotton yarn. Which brand is sold to which merchant group is recorded in detail based on field investigations, which is not without reference value for those engaged in the yarn business. (2) Special attention is paid to the operation of Japanese yarn. Before the boycott, the power of Japanese yarn in Shanghai was greater than that of Chinese yarn. This section pays special attention to the operation of Japanese yarn. In the supply and demand of Shanghai cotton yarn, it is explained that (in terms of quantity, the supply of Shanghai factory yarn is not as good as that of Japanese merchants, but in terms of value, Chinese merchants are far inferior to Japanese merchants,) because Japanese merchants spin fine yarn, while Chinese merchants spin coarse yarn, and the value of the same bale of yarn is very different. In the transportation and sale of Shanghai cotton yarn, it is also explained that the transportation and sale of Chinese cotton yarn is far less common than that of Japanese cotton yarn. In the Shanghai Yarn Factory section, the rise and fall of Chinese and Japanese yarn factories in Shanghai is described, and it is concluded that Chinese factories cannot take advantage of opportunities. In the finance of Shanghai yarn industry, the finance of Chinese and Japanese yarn factories is compared to clarify their strengths and weaknesses. If we want to boycott Japanese goods, we must first understand the reasons for the victory of Japanese goods. This book emphasizes this point in particular and can be used as a reference book for boycotting Japanese yarn. (3) Special attention is also paid to merchant groups who handle yarn. Usually, when talking about the yarn industry, only yarn factories are focused on, and little attention is paid to merchant groups. However, merchant groups control the needs of cotton yarn, and their power should not be underestimated. This book describes the nature, financial transactions, etc. of various merchant groups in detail, and discusses methods for their improvement, which is also rare material.

(4) A very precise exploration of yarn prices. The book plots the yarn prices for the past ten years into a curve, making it clear at a glance, and finds its silver amount to be over 157 taels, and its degree of change to be about ten taels. Therefore, the profits or losses of cotton yarn speculation are deduced, and then the molecules of cotton yarn prices are deduced, and examples are used to prove that all problems with yarn prices are discussed.

The appendix to this section includes a list of yarn factories across the country, a list of Shanghai yarn shops, a list of Shanghai yarn brokers, and a list of Shanghai yarn merchant groups. The material in the entire section is more extensive than the above two sections, and all statistics are quite accurate. Anyone who is concerned about the cotton yarn issue should refer to it. (The three books are sold at the Shanghai Bank Trust Department and the Liming Bookstore on Fourth Malu.)

Current Situation of Japan's National Power Sword Ying

In the more than fifty years since the Meiji Restoration, Japan's national power has leaped to the ranks of the world's powers. Now, it is actually implementing its policy of invading the mainland. In this serious and rapid era of change, the current situation of Japan's national power is what our people urgently need to know.

The current situation of Japan's national power can give us a glimpse of the degree of progress of this enemy and how strong its national life is, as a reference for us. From this, we can know both ourselves and the enemy to decide the direction and plan to deal with the enemy.

The book is divided into nine sections and is extremely concise. The following is a brief introduction.

(1) Area and Population. The total area of Japan's land is more than 44,000 square miles, accounting for one-195th of the world's land. Its recent population is over 91.79 million, and the density is also higher than other countries. The population's occupations are divided into agriculture, fishery, mining, industry, and commerce. On average, 45,000 Japanese from the mainland should be relocated to the colonies every year.

(2) Status of Production and Material Needs. This section describes Japan's important industries, such as agriculture, animal husbandry, forestry, fishery, mining, and industry, and describes the status of each industry, as well as statistics comparing the import and export of goods needed for clothing, food, and housing.

(3) Commerce, Trade, Prices, and Finance. This section describes the general situation of domestic commercial institutions such as exchanges, business companies, warehouses, and various commercial companies. Next, it describes statistics comparing the amount of foreign trade imports and exports. There are also brief descriptions of the balance of payments outside of trade, prices, and financial conditions.

(4) Transportation, Transportation, and Communication. This section describes land transportation (railways, roads, etc.), water transportation (such as shipping, ports, etc.), aviation, and communication institutions, with brief descriptions and statistical comparison tables.

Page 22

(5) National Defense Facilities, Judiciary, and Police. This section describes (1) the current situation of national defense, and includes a table of the current situation of the Japanese army, navy, and air force in Showa 7 (2) describes the situation of the judiciary and police.

(6) Social Facilities. This section describes the establishment of social undertakings, regulations, and institutions, the country's equipment for health care, medicine, and medical affairs, and social sports and general entertainment, etc.

(7) Education, Religion, Academics, Publishing, Literature, Art, and Entertainment. This section briefly describes the characteristics of Japanese education and its spirit and the state of compulsory education, religious beliefs, the progress of academic research, the development of the publishing industry, the imitation and originality of literature and art, and the types of entertainment, which are extremely clear and concise.

(8) Current Situation of Finance. This section describes the national treasury's budget, national debt, local finance, national wealth, and national income, etc., and each item has a brief and concise table.

(9) Conclusion.

The description in this book gives us a most general and simple outline of the current situation of Japan's national power. The conclusion of this book also indicates that the book contains two most obvious meanings. Now I may as well quote them as the end of this introduction. (1) What kind of country is Japan, and what are all its domestic phenomena? This book has given a miniature answer of Japan to these two questions, which can be said to have made a general contribution to those who do not understand Japan. (2) This article can also be said to be a reference with the effect of a catalog for those who aspire to Japanese studies.

Collection of Northeast Immigration Issues

In today's era of turbulent winds and treacherous waves in the Pacific Ocean, the Northeast has simply become the Balkans of the East, and its situation is as serious as that of the Balkans before the war.

The Northeast has a large area and abundant resources, and it is a remote border area, especially under the covetous invasion of Japanese imperialism. The current situation is very dangerous. This is not only a matter of survival in one corner of the Northeast, but the key to the survival of the entire Chinese nation. However, because our country is weak, we cannot use force to resist strong neighbors. Therefore, the best way is to actively colonize the Northeast. This book is for this urgent problem, this great mission to fight for national survival, describing the great significance and practical issues of immigrating to the Northeast, etc. The whole book is divided into five chapters. Now I will briefly introduce it as follows.

(1) The Northeast urgently needs to be developed. This chapter explains that to develop the Northeast, increasing the population is an important issue. The Northeast is a most beautiful and fertile zone recognized by countries around the world today. It is the most suitable agricultural area in the Far East, and its resources are endless.

(2) The great significance of Northeast immigration is divided into two points. From a political point of view, immigration to the border area and self-development can block the path of foreign immigration and preserve the integrity of our country's territorial sovereignty. From an economic point of view, we can only actively invest in rural areas in the Northeast and actively support immigrants to the Northeast.

(3) Investigation of the history of Northeast immigration. This chapter describes the immigration to the Northeast before and during the Qing Dynasty, from the initial form to the land reclamation policy, and the complete abolition of the Manchurian blockade policy.

(4) Modern Northeast Immigration. This section describes the reasons for Northeast immigration in recent years, and analyzes in detail that it is due to overpopulation, natural disasters, wars, bandit disasters, heavy donations, etc. In addition, it also describes the situation of immigration and the state of distribution of immigrants.

(5) Practical Issues of Northeast Immigration. The issues discussed in this chapter all belong to the scope of agriculture. First, the issue of immigrants' financial resources is discussed. Immigrants must have a certain responsible organization to plan and carry out the work, and should raise huge sums of money to subsidize them in order to have practical results. Second, the value of land in recent years has varied greatly due to differences in geology, location, transportation, supply and demand, time, raw or cooked, year, and security conditions. Third, the conditions for renting land by immigrants are described. Fourth, the value of livestock and farm implements in recent years is described. Fifth, the types of hired farmers and the conditions for hired farmers are described. Sixth, the consumption of clothing, food, and housing for immigrants, etc., is described.

The book tells us about the general situation of the Northeast and that immigration is the key to saving the country today. We deeply regret that for decades, we have allowed imperialists and powers to dominate and seize without knowing how to use it or develop it. What a miscalculation this is.
